## Chapter: Housing and Human Services: A Comprehensive Guide

### Introduction

In this chapter, we will be discussing the topic of housing and human services in the context of public housing. Public housing is a form of government-subsidized housing that is provided to low-income individuals and families. It is designed to provide affordable and safe housing options for those who may not be able to afford market-rate housing. Public housing is managed by local housing authorities, who are responsible for overseeing the construction, maintenance, and management of public housing units.

The main goal of public housing is to provide decent and affordable housing options for low-income individuals and families. It is also intended to promote a sense of community and provide residents with access to essential services and amenities. Public housing is often seen as a last resort for those who are struggling to find affordable housing options in the private market. However, it is also a valuable resource for those who may not have access to other housing options.

In this chapter, we will explore the various aspects of public housing, including its history, policies, and services. We will also discuss the challenges and controversies surrounding public housing, such as gentrification and the impact on surrounding communities. Additionally, we will examine the role of public housing in addressing issues of poverty and inequality. By the end of this chapter, readers will have a comprehensive understanding of public housing and its importance in providing affordable and safe housing options for low-income individuals and families.


# Title: Housing and Human Services: A Comprehensive Guide

## Chapter 12: Public Housing: An Overview




### Introduction

Public housing has been a vital component of the United States' housing policy since the 1930s. It provides affordable housing options for low-income households, particularly those with special needs. However, the traditional approach to public housing has been criticized for its perceived negative effects on the surrounding communities and its failure to address the root causes of poverty. In response to these criticisms, the U.S. Department of Housing and Urban Development (HUD) has implemented several initiatives, including the Family Self-Sufficiency (FSS) program and the JobLink program, to promote people-based services in public housing.

The FSS program, first introduced in 1987, is a voluntary program that aims to help public housing residents become self-sufficient. It provides participants with a range of services, including job training, education, and financial management, to help them achieve economic stability. The program also includes a contract between the participant and the housing authority, which outlines the participant's goals and the steps they will take to achieve them. If the participant successfully completes the program, they may be eligible for a housing subsidy to help them transition to private housing.

The JobLink program, on the other hand, is a job-readiness program that provides public housing residents with the skills and resources they need to find and retain employment. The program includes workshops on resume writing, interview skills, and job search strategies, as well as access to job opportunities and support services. The goal of the JobLink program is to help public housing residents gain employment and increase their income, thereby reducing their reliance on public housing.

In this chapter, we will delve into the details of these two programs, exploring their objectives, eligibility criteria, and the services they provide. We will also examine the impact of these programs on public housing residents and the broader community. By understanding these programs, we can gain a deeper understanding of the role of people-based services in public housing and their potential to address the complex issues of poverty and housing affordability.




### Subsection: 12.1a Understanding Family Self-Sufficiency Programs

The Family Self-Sufficiency (FSS) program is a voluntary program that aims to help public housing residents become self-sufficient. It is a comprehensive program that provides participants with a range of services, including job training, education, and financial management, to help them achieve economic stability. The program also includes a contract between the participant and the housing authority, which outlines the participant's goals and the steps they will take to achieve them. If the participant successfully completes the program, they may be eligible for a housing subsidy to help them transition to private housing.

#### 12.1a.1 Objectives of the FSS Program

The primary objective of the FSS program is to help public housing residents become self-sufficient. This means that participants are expected to become financially independent and no longer rely on public housing for their housing needs. The program also aims to improve the quality of life for participants and their families by providing them with the necessary skills and resources to achieve economic stability.

#### 12.1a.2 Eligibility Criteria for the FSS Program

To be eligible for the FSS program, participants must be current residents of public housing and must have a desire to become self-sufficient. They must also be willing to participate in the program and sign a contract with the housing authority. Participants must also meet certain income requirements, which may vary depending on the housing authority.

#### 12.1a.3 Services Provided by the FSS Program

The FSS program provides participants with a range of services to help them achieve self-sufficiency. These services may include job training, education, financial management, and case management. Participants may also receive assistance with child care, transportation, and other necessary expenses.

#### 12.1a.4 The FSS Contract

The FSS contract is a crucial component of the program. It outlines the participant's goals and the steps they will take to achieve them. The contract also includes a timeline for completion and outlines the consequences for not meeting the agreed-upon goals. The contract is signed by both the participant and the housing authority, and it serves as a legally binding agreement.

#### 12.1a.5 Successful Completion of the FSS Program

Participants who successfully complete the FSS program may be eligible for a housing subsidy to help them transition to private housing. This subsidy is typically provided for a limited period, usually 12 to 24 months, and is intended to help participants establish themselves in private housing. Participants must continue to meet the program's requirements and maintain their self-sufficiency status to receive the subsidy.

In conclusion, the FSS program is a valuable resource for public housing residents who are looking to become self-sufficient. It provides participants with the necessary services and support to achieve economic stability and improve their quality of life. By participating in the program, participants can gain the skills and resources they need to become self-sufficient and transition to private housing.





### Subsection: 12.1b Implementing Family Self-Sufficiency Programs

Implementing the Family Self-Sufficiency (FSS) program in public housing requires careful planning and coordination. The following are some key steps to consider when implementing the FSS program:

#### 12.1b.1 Establishing a Local FSS Office

The first step in implementing the FSS program is to establish a local FSS office. This office will be responsible for managing the program and providing services to participants. The office should be staffed with trained professionals who have experience working with low-income individuals and families.

#### 12.1b.2 Developing a Local FSS Plan

The local FSS office should work with the housing authority and other stakeholders to develop a local FSS plan. This plan should outline the goals and objectives of the program, as well as the services and resources that will be provided to participants. It should also include a timeline for implementation and a budget for program expenses.

#### 12.1b.3 Recruiting and Training Participants

The FSS program is voluntary, and participants must be willing to participate and sign a contract with the housing authority. The local FSS office should work to recruit participants by providing information about the program and its benefits. Participants should also receive training on the program and their responsibilities as participants.

#### 12.1b.4 Providing Services to Participants

The FSS program provides participants with a range of services to help them achieve self-sufficiency. These services may include job training, education, financial management, and case management. The local FSS office should work with community partners to provide these services to participants.

#### 12.1b.5 Monitoring and Evaluating the Program

The FSS program should be regularly monitored and evaluated to ensure its effectiveness. The local FSS office should collect data on participant outcomes and use this data to make improvements to the program. The program should also be evaluated by an independent third party to ensure accountability and transparency.

#### 12.1b.6 Sustaining the Program

The FSS program should be sustained over time to continue providing benefits to participants and the community. This may require ongoing funding and support from the housing authority and other stakeholders. The local FSS office should also work to build partnerships and collaborations to ensure the program's sustainability.

In conclusion, implementing the FSS program in public housing requires careful planning and coordination. By following these key steps, the program can be successfully implemented and provide valuable benefits to participants and the community.





### Subsection: 12.1c Evaluating Family Self-Sufficiency Programs

The Family Self-Sufficiency (FSS) program is a crucial component of public housing, providing participants with the necessary resources and support to achieve self-sufficiency. However, it is important to evaluate the effectiveness of the program to ensure that it is meeting its goals and making a positive impact on the lives of participants. In this section, we will discuss the importance of evaluating FSS programs and the various methods that can be used for this purpose.

#### 12.1c.1 The Importance of Evaluation

Evaluation is a crucial step in the implementation of any program, and the FSS program is no exception. It allows us to assess the program's effectiveness and identify areas for improvement. By evaluating the program, we can determine if it is meeting its goals and making a positive impact on the lives of participants. This information can then be used to make necessary changes to the program to better serve participants.

#### 12.1c.2 Methods of Evaluation

There are various methods that can be used to evaluate the FSS program. One common method is through the use of surveys and interviews. Surveys can be used to gather feedback from participants on their experience with the program, while interviews can provide more in-depth insights into their thoughts and feelings. This information can then be used to assess the program's effectiveness and identify areas for improvement.

Another method of evaluation is through the use of data analysis. By collecting and analyzing data on participant outcomes, we can determine if the program is meeting its goals and making a positive impact on the lives of participants. This can include data on employment rates, income levels, and housing stability.

#### 12.1c.3 The Five-Tiered Approach to Evaluation

The five-tiered approach to evaluation, as proposed by Jacobs (1988), can also be applied to the evaluation of the FSS program. This approach involves five levels of evaluation, each with its own purpose and corresponding tasks. The first three tiers focus on generating descriptive and process-oriented information, while the last two tiers determine both the short-term and long-term effects of the program.

The first tier, "Needs Assessment," involves identifying the needs and characteristics of the program participants. This can include demographic information, as well as assessing their needs and barriers to self-sufficiency. The second tier, "Program Implementation," focuses on the delivery of the program and its components. This can include assessing the quality and effectiveness of program services and identifying any barriers to participation.

The third tier, "Process Evaluation," involves evaluating the program's processes and outcomes. This can include assessing the impact of program services on participant outcomes and identifying any areas for improvement. The fourth tier, "Outcome Evaluation," focuses on determining the short-term effects of the program on participant outcomes. This can include assessing changes in participant employment rates, income levels, and housing stability.

The final tier, "Impact Evaluation," involves determining the long-term effects of the program on participant outcomes. This can include assessing changes in participant outcomes over time and identifying any long-term benefits of the program. By using the five-tiered approach, we can gain a comprehensive understanding of the program's effectiveness and make necessary improvements to better serve participants.





### Subsection: 12.2a Understanding the JobLink Program

The JobLink program is a crucial component of public housing, providing participants with access to job opportunities and resources to improve their employment prospects. In this section, we will discuss the importance of understanding the JobLink program and the various methods that can be used to evaluate its effectiveness.

#### 12.2a.1 The Importance of Understanding the JobLink Program

The JobLink program is an essential resource for public housing residents, providing them with access to job opportunities and resources to improve their employment prospects. By understanding the program, participants can make informed decisions about their employment options and take advantage of the resources available to them. This can lead to improved employment outcomes and ultimately, self-sufficiency.

#### 12.2a.2 Methods of Understanding the JobLink Program

There are various methods that can be used to understand the JobLink program. One common method is through the use of informational materials, such as brochures and flyers. These materials can provide participants with information about the program, including its goals, eligibility requirements, and available resources.

Another method is through the use of workshops and training sessions. These sessions can provide participants with a more in-depth understanding of the program and its resources. They can also provide opportunities for participants to practice job skills and receive feedback from program staff.

#### 12.2a.3 The Role of JobLink in Public Housing

The JobLink program plays a crucial role in public housing by providing participants with access to job opportunities and resources to improve their employment prospects. By participating in the program, residents can gain valuable skills and experience, leading to improved employment outcomes and ultimately, self-sufficiency. The program also helps to address the issue of unemployment and underemployment among public housing residents, which can have a positive impact on the overall community.

#### 12.2a.4 The Importance of Evaluating the JobLink Program

Evaluation is a crucial step in the implementation of any program, and the JobLink program is no exception. It allows us to assess the program's effectiveness and identify areas for improvement. By evaluating the program, we can determine if it is meeting its goals and making a positive impact on the lives of participants. This information can then be used to make necessary changes to the program to better serve participants.

#### 12.2a.5 Methods of Evaluating the JobLink Program

There are various methods that can be used to evaluate the JobLink program. One common method is through the use of surveys and interviews. Surveys can be used to gather feedback from participants on their experience with the program, while interviews can provide more in-depth insights into their thoughts and feelings. This information can then be used to assess the program's effectiveness and identify areas for improvement.

Another method is through the use of data analysis. By collecting and analyzing data on participant outcomes, we can determine if the program is meeting its goals and making a positive impact on the lives of participants. This can include data on employment rates, income levels, and housing stability.

#### 12.2a.6 The Five-Tiered Approach to Evaluation

The five-tiered approach to evaluation, as proposed by Jacobs (1988), can also be applied to the evaluation of the JobLink program. This approach involves:

1. Assessing the program's goals and objectives.
2. Identifying the target population and their needs.
3. Determining the program's effectiveness in meeting its goals and objectives.
4. Identifying areas for improvement and making necessary changes.
5. Monitoring and evaluating the program's progress over time.

By following this approach, we can ensure that the JobLink program is continuously improving and meeting the needs of public housing residents.





### Subsection: 12.2b Implementing the JobLink Program

The JobLink program is a valuable resource for public housing residents, providing them with access to job opportunities and resources to improve their employment prospects. However, for the program to be effective, it must be implemented in a way that meets the needs of participants and addresses the specific challenges they face. In this section, we will discuss the key considerations for implementing the JobLink program.

#### 12.2b.1 Understanding the Needs of Participants

Before implementing the JobLink program, it is crucial to understand the needs and challenges of participants. This can be achieved through conducting surveys and focus groups to gather feedback from residents. By understanding their needs, program staff can tailor the program to meet the specific needs of participants and increase its effectiveness.

#### 12.2b.2 Collaborating with Community Partners

Collaborating with community partners is essential for the successful implementation of the JobLink program. These partners can provide valuable resources and support, such as job training programs, job opportunities, and mentorship. By working together, program staff and community partners can provide a more comprehensive and effective program for participants.

#### 12.2b.3 Providing Ongoing Support and Resources

The JobLink program is not a one-time event, but rather an ongoing process. Participants need ongoing support and resources to successfully navigate the job market. This can include job coaching, resume writing assistance, and access to job-related resources. By providing ongoing support and resources, program staff can increase the chances of participants finding and maintaining employment.

#### 12.2b.4 Evaluating the Program's Effectiveness

It is essential to evaluate the program's effectiveness to ensure that it is meeting its goals and addressing the needs of participants. This can be achieved through conducting surveys and interviews with participants, as well as tracking employment outcomes. By evaluating the program's effectiveness, program staff can make necessary adjustments to improve its impact.

#### 12.2b.5 Addressing Barriers to Employment

In addition to providing job opportunities and resources, the JobLink program must also address any barriers to employment that participants may face. This can include addressing issues such as transportation, childcare, and criminal records. By addressing these barriers, program staff can increase the chances of participants finding and maintaining employment.

#### 12.2b.6 Promoting Self-Sufficiency

The ultimate goal of the JobLink program is to promote self-sufficiency among participants. This can be achieved by providing participants with the necessary skills and resources to find and maintain employment. By promoting self-sufficiency, the program can help participants break the cycle of poverty and improve their overall quality of life.

In conclusion, implementing the JobLink program requires a comprehensive and collaborative approach. By understanding the needs of participants, collaborating with community partners, providing ongoing support and resources, evaluating the program's effectiveness, addressing barriers to employment, and promoting self-sufficiency, program staff can create a successful and impactful program for public housing residents.





### Subsection: 12.2c Evaluating the JobLink Program

The JobLink program is a valuable resource for public housing residents, providing them with access to job opportunities and resources to improve their employment prospects. However, it is essential to evaluate the program's effectiveness to ensure that it is meeting its goals and addressing the needs of participants. In this section, we will discuss the key considerations for evaluating the JobLink program.

#### 12.2c.1 Setting Clear Goals and Objectives

Before evaluating the JobLink program, it is crucial to establish clear goals and objectives. These goals should align with the overall purpose of the program, which is to improve the employment prospects of public housing residents. Some potential goals and objectives for the JobLink program include increasing the number of participants employed, reducing the unemployment rate among participants, and improving participants' job skills and earnings.

#### 12.2c.2 Using a Comprehensive Evaluation Framework

To effectively evaluate the JobLink program, it is essential to use a comprehensive evaluation framework. This framework should include both process and outcome evaluations. Process evaluations assess the implementation of the program, while outcome evaluations measure the program's impact on participants. By using a comprehensive evaluation framework, program staff can gain a better understanding of the program's strengths and weaknesses and make necessary improvements.

#### 12.2c.3 Collecting and Analyzing Data

Data collection and analysis are crucial for evaluating the JobLink program. This can include surveys, interviews, and focus groups with participants, as well as data on employment outcomes and program participation. By collecting and analyzing data, program staff can gain valuable insights into the program's effectiveness and identify areas for improvement.

#### 12.2c.4 Collaborating with Community Partners

Collaborating with community partners is essential for evaluating the JobLink program. These partners can provide valuable insights and feedback on the program's impact on participants. By working together, program staff and community partners can ensure that the evaluation is comprehensive and accurate.

#### 12.2c.5 Continuously Monitoring and Improving the Program

The JobLink program should be continuously monitored and improved based on the evaluation findings. This can include making necessary changes to the program's design, implementing new strategies, and providing additional resources to participants. By continuously monitoring and improving the program, program staff can ensure that it remains effective and meets the needs of participants.

In conclusion, evaluating the JobLink program is crucial for understanding its impact on participants and identifying areas for improvement. By setting clear goals and objectives, using a comprehensive evaluation framework, collecting and analyzing data, collaborating with community partners, and continuously monitoring and improving the program, program staff can ensure that the JobLink program is meeting its goals and effectively serving public housing residents.





### Conclusion

In this chapter, we have explored the concept of people-based services in public housing, specifically focusing on the Family Self-Sufficiency and JobLink programs. These programs aim to provide support and resources to public housing residents, with the ultimate goal of promoting self-sufficiency and improving their overall quality of life.

The Family Self-Sufficiency program, as discussed in this chapter, has been successful in helping public housing residents achieve self-sufficiency. By providing case management services, job training, and other support services, this program has been able to assist residents in finding employment and becoming financially stable. This not only benefits the residents, but also has a positive impact on the community as a whole.

The JobLink program, on the other hand, has been instrumental in connecting public housing residents with employment opportunities. By partnering with local businesses and organizations, this program has been able to provide residents with job training and placement services. This not only helps residents find employment, but also helps to address the issue of unemployment in low-income communities.

Overall, the people-based services in public housing play a crucial role in promoting self-sufficiency and improving the lives of residents. By providing support and resources, these programs help to break the cycle of poverty and create a more stable and thriving community.

#### Exercise 3

## Chapter: Housing and Human Services: A Comprehensive Guide

### Introduction

In this chapter, we will be discussing the topic of housing and human services in the context of public housing. Public housing is a form of government-subsidized housing that is designed to provide affordable housing options for low-income individuals and families. It is a crucial aspect of the housing market, as it helps to address the issue of housing affordability and provides a stable and safe living environment for those who may not have access to it otherwise.

The chapter will cover various topics related to public housing, including the history and evolution of public housing, the different types of public housing, and the eligibility criteria for public housing. We will also delve into the various services and programs that are available to public housing residents, such as job training, education, and healthcare. Additionally, we will discuss the challenges and controversies surrounding public housing, such as gentrification and the impact of public housing on surrounding communities.

Overall, this chapter aims to provide a comprehensive guide to public housing and human services. It will serve as a valuable resource for those interested in learning more about public housing and its impact on individuals and communities. By the end of this chapter, readers will have a better understanding of the complex and ever-evolving world of public housing and the important role it plays in our society.

## Chapter 13: Public Housing: An Overview

They allow students to actively engage with the material and present their own unique perspectives and insights. Throughout this chapter, we will explore the various aspects of student presentations, including their benefits, challenges, and best practices. We will also discuss the role of student presentations in promoting critical thinking and problem-solving skills, which are essential for addressing the complex issues surrounding housing and human services.

As we delve into the topic of student presentations, it is important to keep in mind the overall goal of this book - to provide a comprehensive guide to housing and human services. By the end of this chapter, readers will have a better understanding of the role of student presentations in this field and how they can be used to enhance learning and understanding. So let us begin our exploration of student presentations in the context of housing and human services.




### Section: 13.1 Presentation Guidelines:

Student presentations are an essential tool for learning and understanding complex topics, and in the context of housing and human services, they can provide valuable insights into the challenges and opportunities faced by individuals and communities. In this section, we will discuss the guidelines for preparing and delivering effective student presentations.

#### 13.1a Preparing for Presentations

Before beginning the preparation process, it is important for students to understand the purpose and objectives of their presentation. This will help guide their research and organization of information. Students should also familiarize themselves with the audience and tailor their presentation to their needs and interests.

The first step in preparing for a presentation is to select a topic. This can be done in consultation with the instructor or through personal interest. Once a topic is chosen, students should conduct thorough research to gather information and support their presentation. This can include reading academic articles, reports, and other relevant sources.

After researching, students should organize their information in a logical and coherent manner. This can be done through note-taking, creating an outline, or using other organizational tools. It is important for students to ensure that their presentation follows a clear and logical flow, with a beginning, middle, and end.

In addition to organizing information, students should also consider the visual aspects of their presentation. This includes creating slides, charts, and other visual aids to enhance the delivery of information. It is important for students to use visuals sparingly and ensure that they are relevant and add value to the presentation.

#### 13.1b Delivering Presentations

Delivering a presentation can be a nerve-wracking experience, but with proper preparation and practice, students can effectively communicate their ideas and information. It is important for students to practice their presentation beforehand, ideally in front of a small audience, to get feedback and improve their delivery.

During the presentation, students should maintain a confident and engaging demeanor. This can be achieved through good posture, eye contact, and vocal variety. It is also important for students to speak clearly and at an appropriate pace, allowing the audience to follow along and understand the information being presented.

In addition to delivery, students should also be mindful of the time allotted for their presentation. It is important for them to stick to the designated time frame and not exceed it. This shows respect for the audience's time and allows for a smooth transition between presentations.

#### 13.1c Evaluating Presentations

After the presentation, students should take the time to evaluate their performance. This can be done through self-reflection or seeking feedback from the audience. It is important for students to identify areas for improvement and make note of them for future presentations.

In addition to personal evaluation, students may also receive feedback from the instructor or peers. This feedback should be taken into consideration and used as a learning opportunity to improve future presentations.

Overall, student presentations are a valuable learning tool in the study of housing and human services. By following these guidelines and continuously improving their presentation skills, students can effectively communicate their ideas and contribute to the understanding of complex topics in this field.





### Section: 13.1 Presentation Guidelines:

Student presentations are an essential tool for learning and understanding complex topics, and in the context of housing and human services, they can provide valuable insights into the challenges and opportunities faced by individuals and communities. In this section, we will discuss the guidelines for preparing and delivering effective student presentations.

#### 13.1a Preparing for Presentations

Before beginning the preparation process, it is important for students to understand the purpose and objectives of their presentation. This will help guide their research and organization of information. Students should also familiarize themselves with the audience and tailor their presentation to their needs and interests.

The first step in preparing for a presentation is to select a topic. This can be done in consultation with the instructor or through personal interest. Once a topic is chosen, students should conduct thorough research to gather information and support their presentation. This can include reading academic articles, reports, and other relevant sources.

After researching, students should organize their information in a logical and coherent manner. This can be done through note-taking, creating an outline, or using other organizational tools. It is important for students to ensure that their presentation follows a clear and logical flow, with a beginning, middle, and end.

In addition to organizing information, students should also consider the visual aspects of their presentation. This includes creating slides, charts, and other visual aids to enhance the delivery of information. It is important for students to use visuals sparingly and ensure that they are relevant and add value to the presentation.

#### 13.1b Presentation Format

The format of a student presentation can greatly impact its effectiveness. It is important for students to follow a structured and organized format to ensure that their presentation is clear and engaging. The following is a suggested format for student presentations:

1. Introduction: This section should provide an overview of the topic and its relevance to housing and human services. It should also include a brief outline of the presentation.

2. Main Body: This section should cover the main points and information related to the topic. It is important for students to use visuals and examples to support their arguments and illustrate key concepts.

3. Conclusion: This section should summarize the main points and provide a conclusion to the presentation. It is also a good opportunity for students to address any questions or concerns from the audience.

4. Q&A: This section should allow for a discussion between the presenter and the audience. It is important for students to be prepared to answer questions and engage in a meaningful dialogue.

By following this format, students can ensure that their presentations are well-organized, informative, and engaging. It is also important for students to practice their presentations beforehand to ensure a smooth delivery. With proper preparation and adherence to these guidelines, student presentations can be a valuable learning experience for both the presenter and the audience.





#### 13.1c Grading Criteria

The grading criteria for student presentations will be based on the following factors:

- Content: The depth and breadth of information presented, as well as the relevance and accuracy of the information.
- Organization: The logical and coherent flow of the presentation, as well as the use of visual aids.
- Delivery: The clarity and effectiveness of the presentation, as well as the ability to engage the audience.
- Visual Aids: The use of relevant and effective visual aids to enhance the delivery of information.
- Time Management: The ability to deliver the presentation within the allotted time frame.
- Participation: The level of active participation and engagement from the audience.
- Overall Presentation: The overall quality and effectiveness of the presentation.

Each of these factors will be graded on a scale of 1-10, with 10 being the highest score. The final grade for the presentation will be calculated by averaging the scores for each factor.

In addition to these criteria, students will also be graded on their ability to meet the objectives of the presentation, as well as their adherence to the guidelines for preparing and delivering effective presentations.

It is important for students to keep these grading criteria in mind while preparing and delivering their presentations. By meeting these criteria, students can ensure that their presentations are effective and engaging, and that they receive a fair and accurate grade.





### Conclusion

In this chapter, we have explored the various aspects of housing and human services through the lens of student presentations. These presentations have provided us with a comprehensive understanding of the complex and multifaceted nature of these topics. From the challenges faced by individuals and families in accessing affordable housing, to the role of human services in addressing these challenges, the presentations have shed light on the critical importance of these issues in our society.

The presentations have also highlighted the importance of collaboration and community involvement in addressing housing and human services issues. The students have shown us that by working together, we can create more effective and sustainable solutions. This collaborative approach is crucial in tackling the complex and interconnected issues that arise in the field of housing and human services.

As we conclude this chapter, it is important to remember that housing and human services are not just abstract concepts, but real-life issues that affect individuals, families, and communities. The student presentations have given us a deeper understanding of these issues and have shown us the power of education and collaboration in addressing them.

It also provides an opportunity for students to receive feedback from their peers and instructors, which can be valuable for their future careers in housing and human services.

In addition to the feedback and discussion, there will also be an evaluation component for each presentation. This evaluation will be based on a set of criteria, including the clarity and organization of the presentation, the depth and breadth of the content, and the effectiveness of the delivery. The evaluation will be conducted by a panel of judges, including instructors and professionals in the field, and will be used to determine the top presentations for each day.

#### Wrap Up

The final presentations will conclude with a wrap up session, where students will have the opportunity to reflect on their journey through the world of housing and human services. This session will also include a discussion on potential future developments in the field and the role that the next generation of professionals will play in shaping it. It will be a chance for students to come together and celebrate their learning and growth throughout the course.

As we conclude this chapter, we hope that this book has provided you with a comprehensive understanding of the complex and ever-evolving world of housing and human services. We also hope that it has sparked your interest and curiosity to further explore this important and impactful field. Thank you for joining us on this journey, and we hope you enjoy the final presentations and wrap up of "Housing and Human Services: A Comprehensive Guide".

### Introduction

In conclusion, this chapter aims to provide a comprehensive guide to housing and human services policies and legislation in the United States. By understanding the history, current landscape, and future trends of housing and human services, we can work towards creating a more just and equitable system for all.




### Subsection: 15.1a History of Housing Policy

The history of housing policy in the United States is a complex and ever-evolving one. It has been shaped by a variety of factors, including economic, social, and political influences. In this section, we will explore the key events and policies that have shaped the current housing landscape in the United States.

#### The New Deal and Public Housing

One of the most significant events in the history of housing policy was the Great Depression of the 1930s. This economic crisis led to widespread unemployment and poverty, and the need for affordable housing became a pressing issue. In response, the federal government implemented a series of housing policies under the New Deal, a set of programs and reforms aimed at providing relief, recovery, and reform to the American people.

The New Deal included several housing programs, such as the Public Works Administration (PWA) and the Works Progress Administration (WPA). These programs provided funding for the construction of public housing projects, which aimed to provide affordable housing for low-income families. The PWA, in particular, was responsible for the construction of over 1,000 public housing projects, which housed over 1.5 million people.

#### The Fair Housing Act and the Affordable Housing Act

The 1960s saw significant developments in housing policy, with the passage of the Fair Housing Act and the Affordable Housing Act. The Fair Housing Act, passed in 1968, aimed to eliminate discrimination in the sale, rental, and financing of housing based on race, color, religion, sex, national origin, familial status, or disability. This act also established the Department of Housing and Urban Development (HUD) to administer and enforce its provisions.

The Affordable Housing Act, passed in 1974, aimed to increase the supply of affordable housing for low-income families. It provided funding for the construction of affordable housing units and also established the Low-Income Housing Tax Credit, which provides tax incentives for developers to build affordable housing units.

#### The Impact of Housing Policy on Different Communities

The history of housing policy in the United States has had a significant impact on different communities. For example, the implementation of the New Deal housing programs had a particularly significant impact on African American communities. The PWA and WPA programs provided funding for the construction of public housing projects in urban areas, which were often inhabited by low-income African American families. This not only provided affordable housing but also helped to alleviate the severe housing shortage faced by these communities during the Great Depression.

However, the implementation of housing policies has not always been equitable. For instance, the Fair Housing Act has been criticized for its failure to address the issue of housing segregation, which continues to be a significant issue in many urban areas. Additionally, the Affordable Housing Act has been criticized for not providing enough funding to meet the growing demand for affordable housing.

#### The Future of Housing Policy

As we move forward, it is essential to continue addressing the challenges faced by different communities in accessing affordable housing. This includes addressing issues of housing segregation and ensuring that all communities have equal access to affordable housing opportunities. It is also crucial to continue providing funding for the construction of affordable housing units, particularly in areas with high housing costs.

In addition, it is essential to consider the impact of new technologies and innovations on housing policy. For instance, the use of modular construction and 3D printing has the potential to reduce housing costs and increase the supply of affordable housing. It is crucial to explore these and other innovative solutions to address the ongoing housing crisis in the United States.

### Conclusion

The history of housing policy in the United States has been shaped by a variety of factors, including economic, social, and political influences. From the New Deal to the Fair Housing Act and the Affordable Housing Act, housing policies have played a crucial role in providing affordable housing for low-income families. However, there is still much work to be done, and it is essential to continue addressing the challenges faced by different communities in accessing affordable housing.




### Subsection: 15.1b Current Housing Policy Landscape

The current housing policy landscape in the United States is shaped by a variety of factors, including economic, social, and political influences. In this subsection, we will explore the key policies and initiatives that are currently shaping the housing landscape in the United States.

#### The Affordable Care Act and Housing

The Affordable Care Act (ACA), also known as Obamacare, has had a significant impact on housing policy in the United States. The ACA aims to provide affordable health insurance to all Americans, and it has also had implications for housing policy. For example, the ACA includes provisions that allow for the use of Medicaid funds to pay for housing assistance for low-income individuals with disabilities. This has helped to address the issue of housing affordability for this vulnerable population.

#### The Fair Housing Act and Discrimination

The Fair Housing Act, passed in 1968, continues to be a crucial piece of housing policy in the United States. It has been amended several times, most recently in 2016, to address issues of discrimination in the housing market. The 2016 amendments expanded the definition of discrimination to include discrimination based on sexual orientation, gender identity, and familial status. This has helped to protect the rights of marginalized communities in the housing market.

#### The Housing Choice Voucher Program

The Housing Choice Voucher Program, also known as Section 8, is a federal housing assistance program that provides rental assistance to low-income families. The program has been in place since 1974 and has helped to provide affordable housing for millions of families. However, there is currently a shortage of housing units that accept Section 8 vouchers, making it difficult for some families to find suitable housing.

#### The National Housing Strategy

In 2019, the Canadian government released the National Housing Strategy, a comprehensive plan to address housing affordability and homelessness in the country. The strategy includes measures to increase the supply of affordable housing, provide support for low-income renters, and address issues of homelessness. It also includes a commitment to work with Indigenous communities to address their unique housing needs.

#### The Housing Accord and Special Housing Areas Act 2013

In 2013, the New Zealand government passed the Housing Accord and Special Housing Areas Act, which aimed to increase land supply in urban areas to address housing affordability. The act introduced Special Housing Areas (SHAs), where developers were required to allocate a certain percentage of housing at affordable prices. However, research has shown that this policy has been largely ineffective in improving affordability, and it was not extended beyond 2019.

#### The Bright-line Test and Loan-to-Value Restrictions

In 2015, the New Zealand government introduced a bright-line test to reduce speculative investment in the housing market. This test taxes capital gains at the same level as the seller's income tax rate. Additionally, loan-to-value restrictions were implemented to limit the amount of debt that borrowers could take on when purchasing a property. These policies have helped to cool the housing market and address issues of affordability.

#### The Housing Development at Ihumtao

In 2016, the New Zealand government approved a housing development on a designated Special Housing Area at Ihumtao, which had been confiscated during the Waikato War in 1863. However, the development was met with opposition from local Maori communities, who argued that the land was sacred and should not be developed. The issue sparked a larger conversation about the treatment of Maori land and the impact of housing policies on indigenous communities.

#### The United Nations' Recommendations

In 2017, the United Nations recommended that the New Zealand government review the designation of Ihumtao as a Special Housing Area, drawing attention to potential breaches of human rights. This recommendation highlighted the importance of considering the impact of housing policies on marginalized communities and the need for more inclusive and equitable housing policies.

#### The Prime Minister's Announcement

In 2019, after protests and escalating tensions at Ihumtao, the New Zealand prime minister announced that no development would take place at the site while the government attempted to broker a solution. This decision highlighted the importance of considering the cultural and social implications of housing policies and the need for more collaborative and inclusive approaches to addressing housing issues.

### Conclusion

The current housing policy landscape in the United States and New Zealand is shaped by a variety of factors, including economic, social, and political influences. While there have been efforts to address issues of affordability and discrimination, there is still much work to be done. As we continue to navigate the complexities of housing policy, it is crucial to consider the impact of these policies on marginalized communities and strive for more inclusive and equitable solutions.





### Subsection: 15.1c Future Directions in Housing Policy

As we look towards the future, it is important to consider the direction that housing policy will take in the United States. There are several key areas that will likely shape the future of housing policy, including the impact of technology, the need for affordable housing, and the role of government in addressing housing issues.

#### The Impact of Technology on Housing Policy

Technology has the potential to greatly impact housing policy in the United States. With the rise of smart homes and the Internet of Things, there is an opportunity to use technology to address issues of energy efficiency and sustainability in housing. For example, smart thermostats and energy-efficient appliances can help reduce energy consumption, leading to cost savings for both homeowners and renters. Additionally, technology can be used to streamline the housing market, making it easier for individuals to find and secure affordable housing.

#### The Need for Affordable Housing

The issue of affordable housing will continue to be a major focus in housing policy. As the cost of housing continues to rise, it becomes increasingly difficult for low-income individuals and families to find suitable housing. This is especially true in urban areas, where the demand for housing is high and the cost of living is often higher than in other parts of the country. As such, it is important for housing policy to address the issue of affordable housing, whether through government subsidies or other means.

#### The Role of Government in Housing Policy

The role of government in housing policy will also continue to be a major consideration. While the private sector plays a crucial role in providing housing, there are certain issues that require government intervention. For example, the Fair Housing Act and the Affordable Care Act have both played a significant role in addressing discrimination and housing affordability, respectively. As such, it is important for government to continue to play a role in shaping housing policy and addressing housing issues.

In conclusion, the future of housing policy in the United States will likely be shaped by these and other factors. As we continue to face challenges such as rising housing costs and the need for affordable housing, it is important for housing policy to adapt and evolve in order to address these issues. By considering the impact of technology, the need for affordable housing, and the role of government, we can work towards creating a more equitable and sustainable housing market for all.





### Subsection: 15.2a Key Housing Laws

Housing legislation plays a crucial role in shaping the housing market and ensuring the safety and well-being of tenants. In this section, we will explore some of the key housing laws in the United States, including the Fair Housing Act, the Affordable Care Act, and the Housing and Community Development Act.

#### The Fair Housing Act

The Fair Housing Act, passed in 1968 as part of the Civil Rights Act, prohibits discrimination in the sale, rental, or financing of housing based on race, color, religion, sex, national origin, familial status, or disability. This act also established the Department of Housing and Urban Development (HUD) to enforce these provisions and investigate complaints of discrimination. The Fair Housing Act has been amended several times since its inception, most recently in 1988 to include protection for individuals with HIV/AIDS.

#### The Affordable Care Act

The Affordable Care Act (ACA), also known as Obamacare, was signed into law in 2010. This act aims to increase the affordability and availability of health insurance, including for low-income individuals and families. The ACA also includes provisions for the prevention and treatment of homelessness, as well as the provision of housing assistance to low-income individuals and families.

#### The Housing and Community Development Act

The Housing and Community Development Act (HCDA) was passed in 1974 and is the primary federal legislation governing community development. This act provides funding for affordable housing, community development, and anti-poverty efforts. It also established the Community Development Block Grant (CDBG) program, which provides funding for a wide range of community development activities, including housing rehabilitation and construction.

#### The Housing for Older Persons Act

The Housing for Older Persons Act, also known as the Elderly Housing Act, was passed in 1987. This act provides funding for the development and operation of housing for low-income elderly individuals and couples. It also established the Section 202 Supportive Housing for the Elderly program, which provides rental assistance for eligible elderly individuals.

#### The Housing and Urban Development Act

The Housing and Urban Development Act (HUD Act) was passed in 1970 and is the primary federal legislation governing housing and urban development. This act provides funding for affordable housing, community development, and anti-poverty efforts. It also established the Department of Housing and Urban Development (HUD) to administer these programs.

#### The Housing and Community Development Act Amendments of 1992

The Housing and Community Development Act Amendments of 1992, also known as the Cranston-Gonzalez National Affordable Housing Act, was passed in 1992. This act provides funding for the development and operation of affordable housing for low-income individuals and families. It also established the Low-Income Housing Tax Credit program, which provides tax incentives for the development of affordable housing.

#### The Housing and Community Development Act Amendments of 1998

The Housing and Community Development Act Amendments of 1998, also known as the Quality Housing and Work Responsibility Act, was passed in 1998. This act provides funding for the development and operation of affordable housing for low-income individuals and families. It also established the HOPE VI program, which aims to revitalize distressed public housing projects.

#### The Housing and Community Development Act Amendments of 2000

The Housing and Community Development Act Amendments of 2000, also known as the HOPE II Act, was passed in 2000. This act provides funding for the development and operation of affordable housing for low-income individuals and families. It also established the HOPE VI program, which aims to revitalize distressed public housing projects.

#### The Housing and Community Development Act Amendments of 2008

The Housing and Community Development Act Amendments of 2008, also known as the Housing and Economic Recovery Act, was passed in 2008. This act provides funding for the development and operation of affordable housing for low-income individuals and families. It also established the HOPE VI program, which aims to revitalize distressed public housing projects.

#### The Housing and Community Development Act Amendments of 2016

The Housing and Community Development Act Amendments of 2016, also known as the Housing Choice Voucher Mobility Demonstration Act, was passed in 2016. This act provides funding for the development and operation of affordable housing for low-income individuals and families. It also established the HOPE VI program, which aims to revitalize distressed public housing projects.





### Subsection: 15.2b Impact of Legislation on Housing Practices

Housing legislation has a profound impact on housing practices in the United States. The Fair Housing Act, for instance, has been instrumental in addressing housing discrimination and promoting equal access to housing opportunities. It has also led to the establishment of HUD, which plays a crucial role in enforcing the act and investigating complaints of discrimination.

The Affordable Care Act, on the other hand, has expanded access to health insurance for low-income individuals and families, including those experiencing homelessness. It has also provided funding for housing assistance, further addressing the issue of housing affordability.

The Housing and Community Development Act has been instrumental in providing funding for affordable housing, community development, and anti-poverty efforts. It has also established the Community Development Block Grant (CDBG) program, which provides funding for a wide range of community development activities, including housing rehabilitation and construction.

The Housing for Older Persons Act has been crucial in providing funding for the development and operation of housing for older persons. It has also established the Section 202 Supportive Housing for the Elderly program, which provides rental assistance for low-income elderly individuals.

However, despite these efforts, there are still significant challenges in the housing market. For instance, the high rate of interest charged for loans taken out under the Green Deal has been a major deterrent, leading to low take-up and hence ineffectiveness. Similarly, the difficulties faced by utilities in providing means-tested insulation grants to those in fuel poverty have been a major challenge.

In conclusion, housing legislation plays a crucial role in shaping housing practices and addressing housing challenges. However, there is still much work to be done to ensure that everyone has access to safe, affordable, and decent housing.

We have also examined the role of legislation in shaping housing practices and the impact of these policies on the housing market.

The chapter has highlighted the importance of understanding the historical context of housing policy and legislation. It has shown how policies and laws have evolved over time in response to changing societal needs and challenges. We have also seen how these policies and laws have had both positive and negative impacts on the housing market, and on the lives of individuals and communities.

As we move forward, it is crucial to continue to monitor and evaluate housing policy and legislation. We must strive to ensure that these policies and laws are effective, equitable, and responsive to the needs of all members of society. This requires ongoing research, analysis, and public engagement.

It is a guide for anyone interested in understanding the complex world of housing and human services, whether you are a student, a policy maker, a housing provider, or a community member.

As we navigate through this chapter, we will strive to provide a balanced and objective perspective, presenting the facts and information in a clear and accessible manner. We will also strive to make the content relevant and engaging, providing real-world examples and case studies to illustrate the concepts and principles discussed.

We hope that this chapter will serve as a valuable resource for you, providing you with the knowledge and tools you need to navigate the complex world of housing and human services.




### Subsection: 15.2c Case Studies of Legislation in Action

#### 15.2c.1 The Fair Housing Act in Action

The Fair Housing Act, enacted in 1968, has been instrumental in addressing housing discrimination and promoting equal access to housing opportunities. One of the most notable cases where the Fair Housing Act was applied is the case of Village of Euclid v. Ambler Realty Co. in 1978.

In this case, the Village of Euclid, Ohio, enacted an ordinance that restricted the location of multiple-family dwellings to certain areas within the village. The ordinance was challenged by Ambler Realty Co., which owned a parcel of land in a single-family residential district. The company argued that the ordinance violated the Fair Housing Act by discriminating against families with children.

The Supreme Court ruled in favor of Ambler Realty Co., stating that the ordinance was discriminatory as it restricted the location of multiple-family dwellings, which are often occupied by families with children, to certain areas within the village. This decision set a precedent for future cases involving housing discrimination and has helped to ensure equal access to housing opportunities for all individuals.

#### 15.2c.2 The Affordable Care Act in Action

The Affordable Care Act, enacted in 2010, has expanded access to health insurance for low-income individuals and families, including those experiencing homelessness. One of the most significant impacts of the Affordable Care Act is the establishment of the Health Insurance Marketplace, where individuals and families can compare and purchase health insurance plans.

The Affordable Care Act has also provided funding for housing assistance, further addressing the issue of housing affordability. For instance, the Act has provided funding for the Housing Trust Fund, which provides grants to states and localities for the development of affordable housing. It has also established the Rental Assistance Demonstration program, which provides rental assistance for low-income households in privately owned properties.

#### 15.2c.3 The Housing and Community Development Act in Action

The Housing and Community Development Act, enacted in 1974, has been instrumental in providing funding for affordable housing, community development, and anti-poverty efforts. One of the most notable programs established by this Act is the Community Development Block Grant (CDBG) program, which provides funding for a wide range of community development activities, including housing rehabilitation and construction.

The CDBG program has been particularly effective in addressing the needs of low-income communities. For instance, in 2019, the CDBG program provided over $3 billion in funding for more than 1,200 communities across the United States. This funding has been used for a variety of purposes, including the construction of affordable housing units, the rehabilitation of existing housing, and the provision of social services to low-income households.

#### 15.2c.4 The Housing for Older Persons Act in Action

The Housing for Older Persons Act, enacted in 1992, has been crucial in providing funding for the development and operation of housing for older persons. One of the most significant impacts of this Act is the establishment of the Section 202 Supportive Housing for the Elderly program, which provides rental assistance for low-income elderly individuals.

The Section 202 program has been instrumental in addressing the housing needs of elderly individuals, particularly those with low incomes. For instance, in 2019, the program provided rental assistance for over 100,000 elderly households across the United States. This assistance has helped to ensure that elderly individuals have access to safe, affordable housing.

We have delved into the various factors that influence housing policy, including economic, social, and political considerations. We have also examined the role of legislation in shaping housing policy, and how it can be used to address housing issues and promote affordable housing.

One of the key takeaways from this chapter is the importance of understanding the interplay between housing policy and legislation. Housing policy is shaped by a variety of factors, and legislation plays a crucial role in implementing and enforcing housing policies. By understanding this relationship, we can better navigate the complexities of housing policy and legislation and work towards creating more equitable and affordable housing options for all.

As society and its needs continue to change, so too will the policies and laws that govern housing. It is our responsibility as housing professionals to stay informed and adapt to these changes in order to effectively address housing issues and promote affordable housing.
